(4)</div>\n<ul class="NavContent" style="list-style: none none; margin-left: 0; text-align: left; font-size: 105%; margin-top: 0; margin-bottom: 0; line-height: inherit;"><li style="line-height: href="/wiki/File:ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG/280px-ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG" width="280" height="210" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG/420px-ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG/560px-ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ICPO-Interpol_Lione.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interpol headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <b>International Criminal Police Organization</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Organisation internationale de police criminelle</i>; <b>ICPO-INTERPOL</b>), more commonly known as  <b>Interpol</b>, is the <a href="/wiki/International_organization" title="International organization">international organization</a> that facilitates international police cooperation. It was established as the <b>International Criminal Police Commission</b> (<b>ICPC</b>) in 1923; it chose INTERPOL as its <a href="/wiki/Telegraphic_address" title="Telegraphic address">telegraphic address</a> in 1946, and made it its common name in 1956.<sup id="cite_ref-Name_and_logo_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Name_and_logo-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>INTERPOL has an annual budget of around \xe2\x82\xac113 million, most of which is provided through annual contributions by its membership of police forces in 192 countries (as of  2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>). In 2013, the INTERPOL General Secretariat employed a staff of 756, representing 100 member countries.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Its current Secretary-General is <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Stock" title="J\xc3\xbcrgen Stock">J\xc3\xbcrgen Stock</a>, the former deputy head of Germany\'s <a href="/wiki/Federal_Criminal_Police_Office_(Germany)" title="Federal Criminal Police Office (Germany)">Federal Criminal Police Office</a>. He replaced <a href="/wiki/Ronald_Noble" title="Ronald Noble">Ronald Noble</a>, a former United States <a href="/wiki/Under_Secretary_of_the_Treasury_for_Terrorism_and_Financial_Intelligence" title="Under Secretary of the Treasury for Terrorism and Financial Intelligence">Under Secretary of the Treasury for Enforcement</a>, who stepped down in November 2014 after serving 14 years.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> Interpol\'s current President is <a href="/wiki/Meng_Hongwei" title="Meng Hongwei">Meng Hongwei</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Public_Security_(China)" title="Ministry of Public Security (China)">Deputy Minister of Public Security</a> of China.\n</p><p>To keep INTERPOL as politically neutral as possible, its <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">charter</a> forbids it, at least <a href="/wiki/Interpol#Criticism" title="Interpol">in theory</a>, from undertaking interventions or activities of a political, military, religious, or racial nature or involving itself in disputes over such matters.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Its work focuses primarily on public safety and battling transnational <a href="/wiki/Crimes_against_humanity" title="Crimes against humanity">crimes against humanity</a>, <a href="/wiki/Child_pornography" title="Child pornography">child pornography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cybercrime" title="Cybercrime">cybercrime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Drug_trafficking" class="mw-redirect" title="Drug trafficking">drug trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Environmental_crime" title="Environmental crime">environmental crime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Genocide" title="Genocide">genocide</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illicit_drug" class="mw-redirect" title="Illicit drug">illicit drug</a> production,<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Copyright_infringement" title="Copyright infringement">copyright infringement</a>, illicit <a href="/wiki/Trafficking_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect" title="Trafficking (disambiguation)">traffic</a> in <a href="/wiki/Work_of_art" title="Work of art">works of art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Intellectual_Property" class="mw-redirect" title="Intellectual Property">intellectual property crime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Money_laundering" title="Money laundering">money laundering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Organized_crime" title="Organized crime">organized crime</a>, <a href="/wiki/Political_corruption" title="Political corruption">corruption</a>, <a href="/wiki/Terrorism" title="Terrorism">terrorism</a>, <a href="/wiki/War_crimes" class="mw-redirect" title="War crimes">war crimes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Weapons_smuggling" class="mw-redirect" title="Weapons smuggling">weapons smuggling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/White-collar_crime" title="White-collar crime">white-collar crime</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">18</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In the first part of the 20th century, several efforts were taken to formalize international police cooperation, but they initially failed.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> Among these efforts were the First International Criminal Police Congress in <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a> in 1914, and the International Police Conference in New York in 1922. The Monaco Congress failed because it was organized by legal experts and political officials, not by police professionals, while the New York Conference failed to attract international attention.\n</p><p>In 1923, a new initiative was taken at the International Criminal Police Congress in <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">Vienna</a>, where the International Criminal Police Commission (ICPC) was successfully founded as the direct forerunner of INTERPOL. Founding members included police officials from Austria, Germany, Belgium, Poland, China, Egypt, France, Greece, Hungary, Italy, the Netherlands, Romania, Sweden, Switzerland, and <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">Yugoslavia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-faq_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faq-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> The United Kingdom joined in 1928.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The United States did not join Interpol until 1938, although a US police officer unofficially attended the 1923 congress.<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following <i><a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a></i> in 1938, the organization fell under the control of <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, and the Commission\'s headquarters were eventually moved to <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">Berlin</a> in 1942.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> Most members withdrew their support during this period.<sup id="cite_ref-faq_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-faq-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> From 1938 to 1945, the presidents of the ICPC included <a href="/wiki/Otto_Steinh%C3%A4usl" title="Otto Steinh\xc3\xa4usl">Otto Steinh\xc3\xa4usl</a>, <a href="/wiki/Reinhard_Heydrich" title="Reinhard Heydrich">Reinhard Heydrich</a>, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Nebe" title="Arthur Nebe">Arthur Nebe</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ernst_Kaltenbrunner" title="Ernst Kaltenbrunner">Ernst Kaltenbrunner</a>. All were generals in the <a href="/wiki/SS" class="mw-redirect" title="SS">SS</a>, and Kaltenbrunner was the highest ranking SS officer executed after the <a href="/wiki/Nuremberg_Trials" class="mw-redirect" title="Nuremberg Trials">Nuremberg Trials</a>.\n</p><p>After the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> in 1945, the organization was revived as the International Criminal Police Organization by officials from <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scandinavia" title="Scandinavia">Scandinavia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. Its new headquarters were established in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Cloud" title="Saint-Cloud">Saint-Cloud</a>, a suburb of <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>. They remained there until 1989, when they were moved to their present location in <a href="/wiki/Lyon" title="Lyon">Lyon</a>.\n</p><p>Until the 1980s, INTERPOL did not intervene in the prosecution of <a href="/wiki/Nazi" class="mw-redirect" title="Nazi">Nazi</a> <a href="/wiki/War_criminals" class="mw-redirect" title="War criminals">war criminals</a> in accordance with Article 3 of its <a href="/wiki/Constitution" title="Constitution">Charter</a>, which prohibited intervention in "political" matters.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In July 2010, former INTERPOL President <a href="/wiki/Jackie_Selebi" title="Jackie Selebi">Jackie Selebi</a> was found guilty of corruption by the South African <a href="/wiki/High_Courts_of_South_Africa" class="mw-redirect" title="High Courts of South Africa">High Court</a> in Johannesburg for accepting bribes worth \xe2\x82\xac156,000 from a drug trafficker.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> After being charged in January 2008, Selebi resigned as president of INTERPOL and was put on extended leave as National Police Commissioner of South Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> He was temporarily replaced by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Arturo_Herrera_Verdugo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Arturo Herrera Verdugo (page does not exist)">Arturo Herrera Verdugo</a>, the National Commissioner of <a href="/wiki/Investigations_Police_of_Chile" title="Investigations Police of Chile">Investigations Police of Chile</a> and former vice president for the American Zone, who remained acting president until October 2008 and the appointment of <a href="/wiki/Khoo_Boon_Hui" title="Khoo Boon Hui">Khoo Boon Hui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 8 November 2012, the 81st General Assembly closed with the election of Deputy Central Director of the French Judicial Police <a href="/wiki/Mireille_Ballestrazzi" title="Mireille Ballestrazzi">Mireille Ballestrazzi</a> as the first female president of the organization.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In November 2016,  <a href="/wiki/Meng_Hongwei" title="Meng Hongwei">Meng Hongwei</a>, a politician from the People\'s Republic of China, was elected president at the 85th Interpol General Assembly, and will serve in this capacity until 2020.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Constitution">Constitution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Constitution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The role of INTERPOL is defined by the general provisions of its constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-Constitution2008_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Constitution2008-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Article 2 states that its role is:\n</p>\n<ol><li>To ensure and promote the widest possible mutual assistance between all criminal police authorities within the limits of the laws existing in the different countries and in the spirit of the <a href="/wiki/Universal_Declaration_of_Human_Rights" title="Universal Declaration of Human Rights">Universal Declaration of Human Rights</a>.</li>\n<li>To establish and develop all institutions likely to contribute effectively to the prevention and suppression of ordinary law crimes.</li></ol>\n<p>Article 3 states:\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303468">.mw-parser-output .templatequote{overflow:hidden;margin:1em 0;padding:0 40px}.mw-parser-output .templatequote .templatequotecite{line-height:1.5em;text-align:left;padding-left:1.6em;margin-top:0}</style><blockquote class="templatequote"><p>It is strictly forbidden for the Organization to undertake any intervention or activities of a political, military, religious or racial character.\n</p></blockquote>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Methodology">Methodology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Methodology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg/220px-Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg/330px-Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg/440px-Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="385" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Interpol_ID_card_front.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Interpol <a href="/wiki/Identity_document" title="Identity document">ID card</a> (front)</div></div></div>\n<p>Contrary to the way it is frequently portrayed in popular culture, Interpol is not a supranational law enforcement agency and has no agents who are able to make arrests.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Instead, it is an international organization that functions as a network of criminal law enforcement agencies from different countries. The organization thus functions as an administrative liaison among the law enforcement agencies of the member countries, providing communications and database assistance, assisted via the central headquarters in Lyon, France.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Interpol\'s collaborative form of cooperation is useful when fighting international crime because language, cultural and bureaucratic differences can make it difficult for police officials from different nations to work together. For example, if <a href="/wiki/FBI" class="mw-redirect" title="FBI">FBI</a> <a href="/wiki/Special_agents" class="mw-redirect" title="Special agents">special agents</a> track a terrorist to Italy, they may not know whom to contact in the <a href="/wiki/Polizia_di_Stato" title="Polizia di Stato">Polizia di Stato</a>, if the <a href="/wiki/Carabinieri" title="Carabinieri">Carabinieri</a> have jurisdiction over some aspect of the case, or who in the Italian government must be notified of the FBI\'s involvement. The FBI can contact the Interpol National Central Bureau in Italy, which would act as a liaison between the United States and Italian law enforcement agencies.\n</p><p>Interpol\'s databases at the Lyon headquarters can assist law enforcement in fighting international crime.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> While national agencies have their own extensive crime databases, the information rarely extends beyond one nation\'s borders. Interpol\'s databases can track criminals and crime trends around the world, specifically by means of collections of fingerprints and face photos, lists of wanted persons, DNA samples, and travel documents. Interpol\'s lost and stolen travel document database alone contains more than 12 million records. Officials at the headquarters also analyze these data and release information on crime trends to the member countries.\n</p><p>An encrypted Internet-based worldwide communications network allows Interpol agents and member countries to contact each other at any time. Known as I-24/7, the network offers constant access to Interpol\'s databases.<sup id="cite_ref-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclopedia_of_Global_Studies-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> While the National Central Bureaus are the primary access sites to the network, some member countries have expanded it to key areas such as airports and border access points. Member countries can also access each other\'s criminal databases via the I-24/7 system.\n</p><p>Interpol issued 13,637 notices in 2013, of which 8,857 were <a href="/wiki/Interpol_notice" title="Interpol notice">Red Notices</a>, compared to 4,596 in 2008 and 2,037 in 2003. As of  2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, there are currently 52,880 valid notices in circulation.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the event of an international disaster, terrorist attack, or assassination, Interpol can send an Incident Response Team (IRT). IRTs can offer a range of expertise and database access to assist with victim identification, suspect identification, and the dissemination of information to other nations\' law enforcement agencies. In addition, at the request of local authorities, they can act as a central command and logistics operation to coordinate other law enforcement agencies involved in a case. Such teams were deployed eight times in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> Interpol began issuing <a href="/wiki/Interpol_Travel_Document" title="Interpol Travel Document">its own travel documents</a> in 2009 with hopes that nations would remove visa requirements for individuals traveling for Interpol business, thereby improving response times.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> In September 2017, the organization voted to accept <a href="/wiki/State_of_Palestine" title="State of Palestine">Palestine</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> as members.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances"><span id="Foundation"></span>Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2013, Interpol\'s operating income was \xe2\x82\xac78 million, of which 68 percent was contributed by member countries, mostly in the form of statutory contributions (67 percent) and 26 percent came from externally funded projects, private foundations and commercial enterprises. Financial income and reimbursements made up the other six percent of the total.<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> With the goal of enhancing the collaboration between Interpol and the private sector to support Interpol\'s missions, the Interpol Foundation for a Safer World was created in 2013. Although legally independent of Interpol, the relationship between the two is close enough for Interpol\'s president to obtain in 2015 the departure of HSBC CEO from the foundation board after the <a href="/wiki/Swiss_Leaks" title="Swiss Leaks">Swiss Leaks</a> allegations.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>From 2004 to 2010, Interpol\'s <a href="/wiki/External_auditors" class="mw-redirect" title="External auditors">external auditors</a> was the French <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Audit_(France)" title="Court of Audit (France)">Court of Audit</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> In November 2010, the Court of Audit was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Auditor_General_of_Norway" title="Office of the Auditor General of Norway">Office of the Auditor General of Norway</a> for a three-year term with an option for a further three years.<sup id="cite_ref-2011_Financial_Statements_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2011_Financial_Statements-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Criticism">Criticism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Criticism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Despite its politically neutral stance, some have criticized the agency for its role in arrests that critics contend were politically motivated. In the year 2008, the office of the UN High Commissioner for Refugees pointed to the problem of arrests of refugees on the request of Interpol<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> in connection with politically motivated charges. In their declaration, adopted in Oslo (2010),<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> Monaco (2012),<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Istanbul (2013),<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> and Baku (2014),<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> the OSCE Parliamentary Assembly criticized some OSCE member States for their abuse of mechanisms of the international investigation and urged them to support the reform of Interpol in order to avoid politically motivated prosecution. The Istanbul Declaration of the OSCE cited specific cases of such prosecution, including those of the Russian activist Petr Silaev, financier <a href="/wiki/Bill_Browder" title="Bill Browder">William Browder</a>, businessman Ilya Katsnelson, Belarusian politician <a href="/wiki/Ales_Michalevic" title="Ales Michalevic">Ales Michalevic</a>, and Ukrainian politician Bohdan Danylyshyn. The resolution of the Parliamentary Assembly of the Council of Europe of 31 January 2014 criticizes the mechanisms of operation of the Commission for the Control of Interpol\'s files, in particular, non-adversarial procedures and unjust decisions.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, PACE adopted a decision to thoroughly analyse the problem of the abuse of Interpol and to compile a special report on this matter.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> In May 2015, within the framework of the preparation of the report, the PACE Committee on Legal Affairs and Human Rights organized a hearing, during which both representatives of NGOs and Interpol had the opportunity to speak.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Organizations, such as the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Open_Dialog_Foundation&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Open Dialog Foundation (page does not exist)">Open Dialog Foundation</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-en.odfoundation.eu_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.odfoundation.eu-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Fair_Trials_International" class="mw-redirect" title="Fair Trials International">Fair Trials International</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-fairtrials.org_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fairtrials.org-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Centre_for_Peace_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre for Peace Studies">Centre for Peace Studies</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-cms.hr_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cms.hr-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/International_Consortium_of_Investigative_Journalists" title="International Consortium of Investigative Journalists">International Consortium of Investigative Journalists</a><sup id="cite_ref-icij.org_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icij.org-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> indicate that non-democratic states use Interpol in order to harass opposition politicians, journalists, human rights activists and businessmen. According to them, countries that frequently abuse the Interpol system include: China,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> Russia, Iran, Turkey, Kazakhstan, Belarus, Tunisia.<sup id="cite_ref-en.odfoundation.eu_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.odfoundation.eu-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-fairtrials.org_39-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fairtrials.org-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-icij.org_41-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-icij.org-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Open Dialog Foundation\'s report analysed 44 high-profile political cases, which went through the Interpol system.<sup id="cite_ref-en.odfoundation.eu_38-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-en.odfoundation.eu-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> A number of persons who have been granted refugee status in the EU and the US, including: Russian businessman <a href="/wiki/Andrey_Borodin" title="Andrey Borodin">Andrey Borodin</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Chechen Arbi Bugaev,<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> the Kazakh opposition politician <a href="/wiki/Mukhtar_Ablyazov" title="Mukhtar Ablyazov">Mukhtar Ablyazov</a><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> and his associate Artur Trofimov,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> a journalist from Sri Lanka Chandima Withana<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> continue to remain on the public Interpol list. Some of the refugees remain on the list of Interpol even after courts have refused to extradite them to a non-democratic state (for example, Pavel Zabelin,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> a witness in the case of <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Khodorkovsky" title="Mikhail Khodorkovsky">Mikhail Khodorkovsky</a>, Alexandr Pavlov,<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> former security chief of the Kazakh oppositionist <a href="/wiki/Mukhtar_Ablyazov" title="Mukhtar Ablyazov">Ablyazov</a>).\n</p><p>Interpol has recognized some requests to include persons on the wanted list as politically motivated, e.g., Indonesian activist <a href="/wiki/Benny_Wenda" title="Benny Wenda">Benny Wenda</a>, Georgian politician <a href="/wiki/Givi_Targamadze" title="Givi Targamadze">Givi Targamadze</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> ex-president of Georgia <a href="/wiki/Mikheil_Saakashvili" title="Mikheil Saakashvili">Mikheil Saakashvili</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> ex-president of Honduras <a href="/wiki/Manuel_Zelaya_Rosales" class="mw-redirect" title="Manuel Zelaya Rosales">Manuel Zelaya Rosales</a>;<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> these persons have been removed from the wanted list. However, in most cases, Interpol removes a "red notice" against refugees only after an authoritarian state closes a criminal case or declares amnesty (for example, the cases of Russian activists, and political refugees: Petr Silaev, Denis Solopov, Aleksey Makarov, and Turkish sociologist <a href="/wiki/Pinar_Selek" class="mw-redirect" title="Pinar Selek">Pinar Selek</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\nThe election of Meng Hongwei as president and Alexander Prokopchuk, a Russian, as vice president of Interpol for Europe drew criticism in western media and raised fears of Interpol accepting politically motivated requests from China and Russia.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Refugees who are included in the list of Interpol can be arrested when crossing the border.<sup id="cite_ref-fairtrials.org_39-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fairtrials.org-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> The procedure for filing an appeal with Interpol is a long and complex one. For example, the Venezuelan journalist <a href="/wiki/Patricia_Poleo" title="Patricia Poleo">Patricia Poleo</a> and a colleague of Kazakh activist <a href="/wiki/Ablyazov" class="mw-redirect" title="Ablyazov">Ablyazov</a>, Tatiana Paraskevich, who were granted refugee status, sought to overturn the politically motivated request for as long as one and a half years, and six months, respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2013, Interpol was criticised over its multimillion-dollar deals with such private sector bodies as <a href="/wiki/FIFA" title="FIFA">FIFA</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philip_Morris_USA" title="Philip Morris USA">Philip Morris</a>, and the pharmaceutical industry. The criticism was mainly about the lack of transparency and potential conflicts of interest such as <a href="/wiki/Codentify" title="Codentify">Codentify</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup> After the 2015 FIFA scandal, the organization has severed ties with all the private-sector bodies that evoked such criticism, and has adopted a new and transparent financing framework.\n</p><p>In 2016, Taiwan criticised Interpol for turning down Taiwan\'s application to join the General Assembly as an observer.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The United States supports Taiwan\'s participation, and the U.S. Congress passed legislation directing the Secretary of State to develop a strategy to obtain observer status for Taiwan.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://Stockholm%20Center%20for%20Freedom">Stockholm Center for Freedom</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template"><span style="white-space: nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Link_rot" title="Wikipedia:Link rot"><span title="&#160;Dead link since July 2018">permanent dead link</span></a></i>&#93;</span></sup>\'s <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://stockholmcf.org/wp-content/uploads/2017/09/Abuse-Of-The-Interpol-System-By-Turkey_September-20-2017.pdf">report</a> that was issued on September 2017, Turkey has weaponized Interpol mechanisms to hunt down legitimate critics and opponents in violation of Interpol\'s own constitution. The report lists abuse cases where not only arrest warrants but also revocation of travel documents and passports were used by Turkey as persecution tool against critics and opponents. The harassment campaign targeted foreign companies as well.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2014_Russian_intervention_in_Ukraine">2014 Russian intervention in Ukraine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2014 Russian intervention in Ukraine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 25 July 2014, despite Interpol\'s Constitution prohibiting them from undertaking any intervention or activities of a political or military nature,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> the Ukrainian nationalist paramilitary leader <a href="/wiki/Dmytro_Yarosh" title="Dmytro Yarosh">Dmytro Yarosh</a> was placed on Interpol\'s international wanted list at the request of Russian authorities,<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> which made him the only person wanted internationally after the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/2014_Russian_military_intervention_in_Ukraine" class="mw-redirect" title="2014 Russian military intervention in Ukraine">conflict between Ukraine and Russia</a> in 2014. For a long time, Interpol refused to place former <a href="/wiki/President_of_Ukraine" title="President of Ukraine">President of Ukraine</a> <a href="/wiki/Viktor_Yanukovych" title="Viktor Yanukovych">Viktor Yanukovych</a> on the wanted list as a suspect in the mass killing of protesters during <a href="/wiki/Euromaidan" title="Euromaidan">Euromaidan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> Yanukovych was eventually placed on the wanted list on 12 January 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> However, on 16 July 2015, after an intervention of Joseph Hage Aaronson LLP, the British law firm hired by the former Ukrainian President Yanukovych, the international arrest warrant against the former president of Ukraine was suspended pending further review.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> In December 2014, the <a href="/wiki/Security_Service_of_Ukraine" title="Security Service of Ukraine">Security Service of Ukraine</a> (SBU) liquidated a sabotage and reconnaissance group that was led by a former agent of the Ukrainian Bureau of Interpol that also has family relations in the Ukrainian counter-intelligence agencies.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, Russia made attempts to place on the Interpol wanted list Ukrainian politician <a href="/wiki/Ihor_Kolomoyskyi" title="Ihor Kolomoyskyi">Ihor Kolomoyskyi</a> and Ukrainian civic activist Pavel Ushevets, subject to criminal persecution in Russia following his pro-Ukrainian art performance in Moscow.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>According to The Open Dialog Foundation, Russia and other former Soviet republics like Azerbaijan, Belarus and Kazakhstan frequently misuse the Interpol system. The foundation\'s reports cite 44 politically motivated cases which have passed through the Interpol system. Of these, 18 cases originated in Russia, 10 in Kazakhstan and five in Belarus.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_reform_of_Interpol_mechanisms">The reform of Interpol mechanisms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: The reform of Interpol mechanisms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>From 1\xe2\x80\x933 July 2015, Interpol organized a session of the Working Group on the Processing of Information, which was formed specifically in order to verify the mechanisms of information processing. The Working Group heard the recommendations of civil society as regards the reform of the international investigation system and promised to take them into account, in light of possible obstruction or refusal to file crime reports nationally.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Human rights organization, The Open Dialog Foundation, recommended that Interpol, in particular: create mechanism for the protection of rights of people having international refugee status; initiate closer cooperation of the Commission for the Control of Files with human rights NGO and experts on asylum and extradition; enforce sanctions for violations of Interpol\'s rules; strengthen cooperation with NGOs, the UN, OSCE, the PACE and the European Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Fair Trials International proposed to create effective remedies for individuals who are wanted under a Red Notice on unfair charges; to penalize nations which frequently abuse the Interpol system; to ensure more transparency of Interpol\'s work.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Centre for Peace Studies also created recommendations for Interpol, in particular to delete Red Notices and Diffusions for people who were granted refugee status according to 1951 Refugee Convention issued by their countries of origin, and to establish an independent body to review Red Notices on regular basis.<sup id="cite_ref-cms.hr_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cms.hr-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Emblem">Emblem</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Emblem">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:INTERPOL_Logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/INTERPOL_Logo.svg/220px-INTERPOL_Logo.svg.png" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/INTERPOL_Logo.svg/330px-INTERPOL_Logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/d/d9/INTERPOL_Logo.svg/440px-INTERPOL_Logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="331" data-file-height="302" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:INTERPOL_Logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>INTERPOL Emblem</div></div></div>\n<p>The current emblem of Interpol was adopted in 1950 and includes the following elements:<sup id="cite_ref-Name_and_logo_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Name_and_logo-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>the globe indicates worldwide activity</li>\n<li>the olive branches represent peace</li>\n<li>the sword represents police action</li>\n<li>the scales signify justice</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Members">Members</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a />&#160;</span><a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a></li></ul></div> \n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Offices">Offices</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Offices">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In addition to its General Secretariat headquarters in Lyon, Interpol maintains seven regional bureaus:<sup id="cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Buenos_Aires" title="Buenos Aires">Buenos Aires</a>, <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">Argentina</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/San_Salvador" title="San Salvador">San Salvador</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">El Salvador</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9" title="Yaound\xc3\xa9">Yaound\xc3\xa9</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Abidjan" title="Abidjan">Abidjan</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B4te_d%27Ivoire" class="mw-redirect" title="C\xc3\xb4te d&#39;Ivoire">C\xc3\xb4te d\'Ivoire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Nairobi" title="Nairobi">Nairobi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya" title="Kenya">Kenya</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Harare" title="Harare">Harare</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zimbabwe" title="Zimbabwe">Zimbabwe</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bangkok" title="Bangkok">Bangkok</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a> (Liaison Office)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, Brussels Liaison office</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Den_Haag" class="mw-redirect" title="Den Haag">Den Haag</a> Europol</li></ul>\n<p>Interpol\'s Command and Coordination Centres offer a 24/7 point of contact for national police forces seeking urgent information or facing a crisis. The original is in Lyon with a second in Buenos Aires added in September 2011. A third was opened in Singapore in September 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Interpol opened a Special Representative Office to the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York</a> in 2004<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> and to the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a> in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The organization has constructed the Interpol Global Complex for Innovation (IGCI) in Singapore to act as its <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a> facility, and a place of cooperation on digital crimes investigations. It was officially opened in April 2015, but had already become active beforehand. Most notably, a worldwide takedown of the SIMDA botnet infrastructure was co-ordinated and executed from IGCI\'s Cyber Fusion Centre in the weeks before the opening, as was revealed at the launch event.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Secretaries-general_and_presidents">Secretaries-general and presidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Secretaries-general and presidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-84"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-84">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Taiwan was an Interpol member as the Republic of China until 1984, when it was replaced by the People\'s Republic of China. Taiwan was offered an option to continue as China\'s sub-bureau under name "Taiwan, China", but as this could imply that Taiwan was part of the People\'s Republic of China, it refused and withdrew from the organization.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Interpol&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2013_Annual_Report-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-3"><sup><i><b>d</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-4"><sup><i><b>e</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-2013_Annual_Report_1-5"><sup><i><b>f</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.interpol.int/content/download/25671/352500/version/4/file/INTERPOL%20Annual%20Report%202013_EN_LR.pdf">"Annual Report 2013"</a> <span class="cs1-format">(PDF)</span>.
